  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer10706934084445941123">The year is 50BC, and all Gaul is occupied. Only one small village of indomitable Gauls still holds out against the invaders. But how much longer can Asterix, Obelix and their friends resist the mighty Roman legions of Julius Caesar? Anything is possible, with a little cunning plus the druid Getafix's magic potions! <span id="freeTextContainer5561085794271004986">Astérix le Gaulois = Asterix the Gaul (Asterix, #1), René Goscinny<br/><br/>Asterix the Gaul is the first volume of the Asterix comic strip series, by René Goscinny (stories) and Albert Uderzo (illustrations). <br/><br/>All Gaul is under Roman control, except for one small village in Armorica (present-day Brittany), whose inhabitants are made invincible by a magic potion created periodically by the Druid Getafix. To discover the secret of the Gauls' strength, Centurion Crismus Bonus, commander of a Roman garrison a</span>
  <span id="freeText5561085794271004986" style="display:none">Astérix le Gaulois = Asterix the Gaul (Asterix, #1), René Goscinny<br /><br />Asterix the Gaul is the first volume of the Asterix comic strip series, by René Goscinny (stories) and Albert Uderzo (illustrations). <br /><br />All Gaul is under Roman control, except for one small village in Armorica (present-day Brittany), whose inhabitants are made invincible by a magic potion created periodically by the Druid Getafix. To discover the secret of the Gauls' strength, Centurion Crismus Bonus, commander of a Roman garrison at the fortified camp of Compendium, sends a spy disguised as a Gaul into the village. The Roman's identity is revealed when he loses his false moustache, shortly after he discovers the existence of the magic potion; whereupon he reports his discovery to the Centurion. ..<br /><br />عنوانها: آستریکس قهرمان گال؛ آستریکس در سرزمین گل؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز دوم ماه می سال 2004 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: ماجراهای آستریکس و ابیلیکس کتاب 01 - آستریکس قهرمان گال؛ نویسنده: رنه گوسینی؛ مترجم: مهدی شاه خلیلی؛ تهران، لک لک، 1381؛ از ماجراهای آستریکس و ابیلیکس کتاب 01؛ در 48ص؛ مصور رنگی؛ گروه سنی ج د؛ شابک 9646488471؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، تاریخ فرهنگ، 1383؛ شابک ایکس - 964713567؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، کلام، 1385؛ شابک 9646143695؛ موضوع داستانهای فکاهی مصور از نویسندگان فرانسوی سده 20 م<br /><br />عنوان: آستریکس در سرزمین گل؛ نویسنده رنه گوسینی؛ مترجم فریبرز افروزی؛ تهران، سامر، 1390؛ در 48ص؛ گروه سنی ج د؛ شابک 9786006444000؛<br /><br />گال در تصرف رمیهایت؛ بجز یک دهکده کوچک در آرمورکا (بریتانیای امروزی)؛<br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6938006433792318920"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303171i/17120100.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>A kindred spirit...<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303171i/17120102._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Family portrait.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303539i/17120119._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Sport/recreation/favorite pastime.<br/><br/>=========<br/><br/>For those not familiar with the Asterix comics, let me give you a bit of background, both personal and general.<br/><br/>Let me start with Julius Caesar. <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358525i/17129536._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>We all know him, eh? And most of us probably know that Ceasar defeated the Gauls, thereby incidentally Latinizing and unifying them. <br/><br/>After conquering and annexing Gaul with a two-year war, fought from 52 to 50 BC, he did actually see a small rebellion, though not quite of </span>
  <span id="freeText6938006433792318920" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303171i/17120100.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>A kindred spirit...<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303171i/17120102._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Family portrait.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448303539i/17120119._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Sport/recreation/favorite pastime.<br><br>=========<br><br>For those not familiar with the Asterix comics, let me give you a bit of background, both personal and general.<br><br>Let me start with Julius Caesar. <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358525i/17129536._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>We all know him, eh? And most of us probably know that Ceasar defeated the Gauls, thereby incidentally Latinizing and unifying them. <br><br>After conquering and annexing Gaul with a two-year war, fought from 52 to 50 BC, he did actually see a small rebellion, though not quite of the kind we encounter in the Asterix comix.<br><br>The Asterix comics are funny, despite the violence depicted in them, for a few reasons. I normally don’t find slapstick comedy amusing at all, but here it is funny because of the wild improbability of a small little runt like Asterix - your typical weakling brainy nerd stereotype, beating up those brawny armored Romans. <br><br>What is his secret? Similar to Achilles who was dipped into the River Styx which gave him superhuman strength/invulnerability, Asterix’s friend Obelix had as a baby, fallen into a cauldron of magic potion as brewed by the village bard, Getafix; the same magic potion that gives Asterix and the rest of his village superhuman qualities for a limited time after consumption.<br><br>And so, Asterix’s village turns out to have been poor old Ceasar’s secret nightmare - the Gaulish village he couldn’t conquer! Of course this whole concept is pretty fun from a French-person’s point of view.<br>The authors riff on many things through the course of the comics. One of them, for example, the way that the French are always going : “Nos ancêtres les Gaulois!” [Our ancestors the Gauls!]<br><br>There is constant play with how the Gauls’ names ended in the suffix “ix” (for example, one of their great leaders was named Vercingetorix), hence, in the Asterix comics, the druid is named Getafix, <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358447i/17129531.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> the big guy who carries a menhir or Obelisk around is called Obelix, the village bard is called Cacofonix, <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358223i/17129505.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358224i/17129506.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358224i/17129507.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>(poor old Cacofonix - nobody ever appreciates his art - those barbarians!)<br>The fishmonger who always has smelly fish, is called Unhygenix, and the little dog is called Dogmatix. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448358525i/17129537.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> Asterix in front, Obelix at back, and Dogmatix - middle.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6938006433792318920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249301907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16297858359844952041"><b><br/><br/>another UPDATE at bottom</b><br/><br/>I got this over Christmas 2014, when I saw some lying in a book store. There are (according to a list inside the front cover) 33 Books available in English translation, available singly or in Omnibus editions of 3 Books each.<br/><br/>I glanced at it, browsing a bit as it lay on the table in my family room for months. Amusing.<br/><br/>I had really picked it up for my grandson, who's just turned seven. But when I tried to interest him in it, he was not very enthusiastic. Perhaps he saw a bun</span>
  <span id="freeText16297858359844952041" style="display:none"><b><br /><br />another UPDATE at bottom</b><br /><br />I got this over Christmas 2014, when I saw some lying in a book store. There are (according to a list inside the front cover) 33 Books available in English translation, available singly or in Omnibus editions of 3 Books each.<br /><br />I glanced at it, browsing a bit as it lay on the table in my family room for months. Amusing.<br /><br />I had really picked it up for my grandson, who's just turned seven. But when I tried to interest him in it, he was not very enthusiastic. Perhaps he saw a bunch or words he didn't understand? Strange punny Latin character names, even Latin words? Whatever.<br /><br />Finally a couple evenings ago I sat down and read it through. Of course that's what's intended, and it improved. Many laughs, though I'm sure I missed quite a bit because of the Latin stuff, even though I probably have more Latin than most Americans.<br /><br />And maybe my grandson, when a little older, will want to read it. Though perhaps it's just as well that he didn't fall in love with it and want more, they're quite dear in the U.S.<br /><br />If he'd liked it, I'd probably round up to a four.<br /><br />And how about my granddaughter? She's older (ten), but not here so often. (Too many athletic interests.) I'll have to try it, and she is a reader. She says she's tried Harry Potter and didn't like it ... but loves the Hunger Games books. How would one predict re Asterix from that? Don't know. <br /><br /><b>UPDATE</b> My grandson here with me tells me he DID like it, but there were some hard words in it. SO I'm updating it to 4 stars and we will be looking at it together in the future.<br /><br /><b>another UPDATE</b> Grandson now 9. He'd rather play games (board &amp; electronic) than read right now. He plays the viola, and before he turned 9 last month had most swimming records in MD-VA-DC for his age. He's very good, if I do say so. So is his 12-year old sister, though she might be a better runner than swimmer, and might be a more popular and more caring young girl than those accomplishments. I'm blessed.</span>

<div id="review_1317110207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1317110207" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16077597-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582900704p2/16077597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1317110207?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/16077597-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/81350.Asterix_der_Gallier">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16077597-matt?shelf=look-out-kid">look-out-kid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16077597-matt?shelf=comic-book-and-me">comic-book-and-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16077597-matt?shelf=it-takes-a-lot-to-laugh">it-takes-a-lot-to-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1317110207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13644697884052527152"><b>+++ BREAKING +++</b><br/><br/>(Berlin) Is this the end of the indomitable Gauls? <br/>Ehapa publishing house announced on Wednesday, that all volumes of the popular Asterix series of author René Goscinny and illustrator Albert Uderzo will be immediately removed from trade. The publisher responds to an inquiry by the National Anti-Doping Agency (NADA) in Germany, who was able to demonstrate years of extensive doping of the popular cartoon characters. At the end of last week, the NADA had published their results. Ac</span>
  <span id="freeText13644697884052527152" style="display:none"><b>+++ BREAKING +++</b><br><br>(Berlin) Is this the end of the indomitable Gauls? <br>Ehapa publishing house announced on Wednesday, that all volumes of the popular Asterix series of author René Goscinny and illustrator Albert Uderzo will be immediately removed from trade. The publisher responds to an inquiry by the National Anti-Doping Agency (NADA) in Germany, who was able to demonstrate years of extensive doping of the popular cartoon characters. At the end of last week, the NADA had published their results. According to those, NADA inspectors were able to proof the use of an illegal substance, euphemistically called "Magic Potion", in all of the booklets. The infamous doping doctor Getafix (a.k.a "Magigamix", a.k.a "The Druid") has apparently manipulated blatantly and unabashedly all the beatings and battle results of the Gauls against Roman patrols, field camps and legions. This is considered gross unsporting conduct with no trace of a fair competition. In a statement issued by the agency it's said: "We fear that the glorification of the doping agent as 'magic potion' without side effects decreases the threshold for the use of performance-enhancing substances and especially younger readers are at risk". Particularly shocking: A character is said to have fallen into the doping substance as a child and since then had superhuman powers. Ehapa publishing meanwhile remains contrite and leaves the future of the popular comics open. According to a spokesman a re-launch of the series is planned, but whether or not the new volume, tentatively called "Asterix and the destruction of the small village by obviously vastly superior Romans", will make its way to the German books shops is still open.<br><br>[this is a free translation of <a href="http://www.der-postillon.com/2014/07/asterix-comics-wegen-doping-verdachts.html" rel="nofollow noopener">an article</a> from German news channel <em>Der Postillon</em> (honest news, independent, fast, since 1845)]<br><br>______________________________<br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380148217i/680962.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This work is licensed under a <a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/" rel="nofollow noopener">Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13644697884052527152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_96791514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96791514" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96791514?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96791514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4882329280232375332"><br/>As far as I’m concerned this is a good news / better news scenario:<br/><br/><u>The Good News</u><br/><br/>Between the nostalgia and the clever wordplay, what’s not to like? The artwork isn’t as polished as later entries, but it’s still awesome. I particularly enjoyed the hair puns, and few artists can convey infectious laughter through their drawings like Albert Uderzo was able to. Of course, it helps if you have a bit of general knowledge, to more appreciate the satiric aspects of the comedy. This is the first Asterix b</span>
  <span id="freeText4882329280232375332" style="display:none"><br />As far as I’m concerned this is a good news / better news scenario:<br /><br /><u>The Good News</u><br /><br />Between the nostalgia and the clever wordplay, what’s not to like? The artwork isn’t as polished as later entries, but it’s still awesome. I particularly enjoyed the hair puns, and few artists can convey infectious laughter through their drawings like Albert Uderzo was able to. Of course, it helps if you have a bit of general knowledge, to more appreciate the satiric aspects of the comedy. This is the first Asterix book, and while a few characters are introduced, the only two characters that <i>really</i> feature are Asterix himself and Getafix the druid. Which brings me to…<br /><br /><u>The Better News</u><br /><br />If you enjoyed this book, there are many more where it came from. Almost all of the Asterix books are really cool. Personally, I think Uderzo did a remarkable job keeping the series alive after Goscinny’s passing in 1977 (you may be surprised to see which entries were published with only Uderzo at the helm, even though Goscinny’s name still appeared on the cover).<br />It’s only toward the latter end of the series that there is a bit of a dip. In my personal opinion it’s only really in the mid-2000’s (with Asterix &amp; The Falling Sky) that things went a bit awry. <br /><br />Here’s to almost 60 years of Asterix!<br /><br />5 stars and then some.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=humour">humour</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541938280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9633563279260313263">By Toutatis! Everyone should read this beginning book of a brilliant series! We finally purchased the entire Asterix set in 2019, so I intend to read through the series this year. <br/><br/>When a Roman soldier infiltrates the Gaulish village, he is able to provide information about the magic potion to the Romans, which leads to Getafix being kidnapped. Asterix sets out to free him all alone, without even the help of the magic potion. This story mainly involves Asterix and Getafix, who get into all kinds </span>
  <span id="freeText9633563279260313263" style="display:none">By Toutatis! Everyone should read this beginning book of a brilliant series! We finally purchased the entire Asterix set in 2019, so I intend to read through the series this year. <br /><br />When a Roman soldier infiltrates the Gaulish village, he is able to provide information about the magic potion to the Romans, which leads to Getafix being kidnapped. Asterix sets out to free him all alone, without even the help of the magic potion. This story mainly involves Asterix and Getafix, who get into all kinds of adventures together. <br /><br />There are only a very few characters in this book, and the village crowd have not yet appeared. We only meet Asterix, Obelix, Vitalstatistix, Cacofanix and Getafix. But we get to meet the Romans and Julius Caesar himself. <br /><br />I am always left dazed by the brilliance of the puns in this series, and this first effort was no different. The English translation also complements the original French so effortlessly that it's a completely different level of genius. <br /><br />Plan to read all the books in order again, this time in English.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7967975139029354867">Reading so much serious literature lately, this old classic felt like a fun indulgence on a beautiful spring day in the balcony. It took me back to my childhood when I would read and reread the series. It was just as good, I actually laughed out loud a few times and my neighbor turned my way wondering if I had a few screws loose.<br/><br/></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_111791336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111791336" />
    <a title="Bruce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/897874-bruce"><img alt="Bruce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202929351p2/897874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111791336?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce" href="/user/show/897874-bruce">Bruce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111791336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2993668419712922858">Well, *have* you read all the Asterix books? It's a fair question. We've read these, but these aren't all. There are, in fact, at least 8 not identified here. Quick quiz Asterix fans - can you name them without resorting to internet memory? <span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>I had the tremendous good fortune to find all but a few of the published volumes in one of our local libraries, and to be able to borrow the remainder of those I could not find from a friend who collects them. If you've yet to be introduced to th</span>
  <span id="freeText2993668419712922858" style="display:none">Well, *have* you read all the Asterix books? It's a fair question. We've read these, but these aren't all. There are, in fact, at least 8 not identified here. Quick quiz Asterix fans - can you name them without resorting to internet memory? <span>[image error]</span><br><br>I had the tremendous good fortune to find all but a few of the published volumes in one of our local libraries, and to be able to borrow the remainder of those I could not find from a friend who collects them. If you've yet to be introduced to these intrepid Gaulish warriors, you really owe it to yourself to run out and find one of these books.<br><br>For starters, if you have kids who can read, having one of these to hand will make you their temporary hero. But the artwork on display is tremendous (see, e.g., <span>[image error]</span> - this is a page from "Asterix &amp; the Laurel Wreath" and -- in the second row -- pulls off the amazing task of stopping and running your mental camera backward. Behold, the semiotic power of comics!); the humor unabating; and the social, political, and historical satire merciless and timeless.<br><br>It's a pity author Goscinny died so young. His creative partner Uderzo, while a wonderful artist, was not that much of a plotter or writer. The books he completed in the 30 years following his partner's tragic demise in the mid-70s aren't nearly as powerful as their predecessors. Since 2001, Pathe has taken to making live-action extravaganzas out of these (at least three to date), and starring no less a thespian than Gerard Depardieu, but as of this writing they are yet to be released in the states, nor does Netflix carry them. Somebody with pull fix this!<br><br>Seriously, I can't rave about these books enough, whether written in Latin, their original French, or here in these hysterical English translations. Here's my nutshell summary of the complete Asterix and Obelix bibliography.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71292.Asterix_the_Gaul__Asterix___1_" title="Asterix the Gaul (Asterix, #1) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Gaul</a> – introducing A&amp;O in their milieu, facing Caesar for the first time<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122439.Asterix_and_the_Golden_Sickle__Asterix___2_" title="Asterix and the Golden Sickle (Asterix, #2) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Golden Sickle</a> – A&amp;O go to Lutetia (Paris) to buy Druid Getafix a new sickle (takes on protection rackets)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122408.Asterix_and_the_Goths__Asterix___3_" title="Asterix and the Goths (Asterix, #3) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Goths</a> – endless early Germanic intratribal warfare explained when the Goths take Getafix hostage across the Rhine<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122401.Asterix_the_Gladiator__Asterix___4_" title="Asterix the Gladiator (Asterix, #4) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Gladiator</a> – A&amp;O go to Rome to free captured bard Cacofonix; a terrific spoof of Spartacus, among other things<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122421.Asterix_and_the_Banquet__Asterix___5_" title="Asterix and the Banquet (Asterix, #5) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Banquet</a> – A&amp;O do the first Tour de France to win a culinary/military bet against the Romans<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122410.Asterix_and_Cleopatra__Asterix___6_" title="Asterix and Cleopatra (Asterix, #6) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix Cleopatra</a> – A&amp;O in Alexandria when an Egyptian architect enlists Getafix’s help proving to the Romans that Egyptian culture is still all that<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122404.Asterix_and_the_Big_Fight__Asterix___7_" title="Asterix and the Big Fight (Asterix, #7) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Big Fight</a> – the Romans have a Gaulish chieftain-collaborator challenge Chief Vitalstatistix to a winner-takes-all bare-knuckle brawl… and Getafix is out of magic potion! Terrific send up of proxy warfare (to say nothing of professional wrestling)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71299.Asterix_in_Britain__Asterix___8_" title="Asterix in Britain (Asterix, #8) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix in Britain</a> – A&amp;O find nothing better to do than help their cousin Celts beat back the Roman suppressing forces<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122420.Asterix_and_the_Normans__Asterix___9_" title="Asterix and the Normans (Asterix, #9) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Normans</a> – teenaged Justforkix helps teach the Norse the true meaning of fear. Extremely clever investigation into the psychology of thrill-seeking<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122418.Asterix_the_Legionary__Asterix___10_" title="Asterix the Legionary (Asterix, #10) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Legionary</a> – A&amp;O enlist to rescue Panacea’s impressed beau. Shades of Billy Budd?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122403.Asterix_and_the_Chieftain_s_Shield__Asterix___11_" title="Asterix and the Chieftain's Shield (Asterix, #11) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Chieftain's Shield</a> – Turns out Chief Vitalstatistix has been riding around on Vercingetorix’ forfeited shield; what alternate proof can Caesar use in a Gaulish triumph?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71298.Asterix_at_the_Olympic_Games__Asterix___12_" title="Asterix at the Olympic Games (Asterix, #12) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix at the Olympic Games</a> – was use of the magic potion at the original games the first instance of doping?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122437.Asterix_and_the_Cauldron__Asterix___13_" title="Asterix and the Cauldron (Asterix, #13) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Cauldron</a> – A&amp;O learns the economics of labor as they are forced to earn back a cauldron of sesterces stolen on their watch; bright spoof of Milton Friedman’s and John Maynard Keynes’ theories (see also “Obelix &amp; Co.,” below)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122440.Ast_rix_in_Spain__Asterix___14_" title="Astérix in Spain (Asterix, #14) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix in Spain</a> – A&amp;O travel to raise a Roman siege against a small Spanish village on behalf of an Iberian chieftain’s son<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122441.Asterix_and_the_Roman_Agent__Asterix___15_" title="Asterix and the Roman Agent (Asterix, #15) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Roman Agent</a> – the denizens of our favorite village have to contend with an insidious new Roman tactician: a rumor-mongering, scandalous slanderer! A marvelous study of envy and petty jealousy<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122438.Asterix_in_Switzerland__Asterix___16_" title="Asterix in Switzerland (Asterix, #16) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix in Switzerland</a> – A&amp;O are off to Helvetia to pluck some much-needed Edelweiss<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71296.The_Mansions_of_the_Gods__Asterix___17_" title="The Mansions of the Gods (Asterix, #17) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mansions of the Gods</a> – As the Roman’s sponsor a neighboring suburban development, can our favorite villagers resist the corrupting temptations of modernity? Terrific satire of assimilation and upward-mobility<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122413.Asterix_and_the_Laurel_Wreath__Asterix___18_" title="Asterix and the Laurel Wreath (Asterix, #18) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Laurel Wreath</a> – A&amp;O become Roman house slaves in an attempt to steal Caesar’s laurel’s for soup flavoring (to help Vitalstatistix save face from a stupid wager); a clever look at the household economy of your average well-to-do Roman citizen<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71300.Asterix_and_the_Soothsayer__Asterix___19_" title="Asterix and the Soothsayer (Asterix, #19) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Soothsayer</a> – Asterix sets out to expose a peripatetic fraud playing on the credulity of his friends<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71297.Asterix_in_Corsica__Asterix___20_" title="Asterix in Corsica (Asterix, #20) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix in Corsica</a> – A&amp;O provide an escaped Roman hostage safe passage back home. A spoof of either Corsican tribalism or the mafia… probably both.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122405.Asterix_and_Caesar_s_Gift__Asterix___21_" title="Asterix and Caesar's Gift (Asterix, #21) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix Caesar's Gift</a> – big spoof of the political “silly season” as several candidates campaign to be the village’s next chief, sparked originally by Caesar’s mischievious deed of the village land to a no-account legionary (see also “Great Divide,” below)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71293.Asterix_and_the_Great_Crossing__Asterix___22_" title="Asterix and the Great Crossing (Asterix, #22) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Great Crossing</a> – a freak storm blows A&amp;O (on an impromptu fishing trip) and a longboat full of Norse explorers across the Atlantic Ocean<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71301.Obelix_and_Co___Asterix___23_" title="Obelix and Co. (Asterix, #23) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Obelix Co.</a> – an excellent companion to “Cauldron,” flipping the premise to the side of capital; as a recent Roman business school grad prompts Obelix to mass-produce menhirs for Roman consumption<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81332.Asterix_in_Belgium__Asterix___24_" title="Asterix in Belgium (Asterix, #24) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix in Belgium</a> – A&amp;O set off to Belgica to determine whom the local legionaries less like to fight, Gaulish or Belgian warriors<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122449.Asterix_and_the_Great_Divide__Asterix__25_" title="Asterix and the Great Divide (Asterix #25) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Great Divide</a> – an excellent companion to “Caesar’s Gift,” this one analogizes two-party governance to a Romeo &amp; Juliet-style feud, as Druid Getafix calls upon a village that’s literally split right down the middle by competing co-chieftains<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122444.Asterix_and_the_Black_Gold__Asterix___26_" title="Asterix and the Black Gold (Asterix, #26) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Black Gold</a> – A&amp;O nearly die of exposure in the Arabian desert trying to obtain some “rock oil” for Getafix; prompting modern readers to ask, what good is this <i>petra oleum</i>, anyway?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122447.Asterix_and_Son__Asterix__27_" title="Asterix and Son (Asterix #27) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix Son</a> – the best and least muddled of artist Uderzo’s solo attempts, Cleopatra secretly hides newborn baby Caesarion from Caesar’s adopted son Brutus among our Gaulish friends<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122448.Asterix_and_the_Magic_Carpet__Asterix__28_" title="Asterix and the Magic Carpet (Asterix #28) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Magic Carpet</a> – a mediocre Uderzo plot that serves as an excuse for exquisite artwork (the ancient world from above); Cacofonix is flown by magic carpet from Gaul to a parched land of the Ganges in the hopes his horrible singing will summon a delinquent monsoon<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122443.Asterix_and_the_Secret_Weapon__Asterix__29_" title="Asterix and the Secret Weapon (Asterix #29) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Secret Weapon</a> – haven’t gotten my hands on this one yet!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1216815.Asterix_and_Obelix_All_at_Sea__Asterix__30_" title="Asterix and Obelix All at Sea (Asterix #30) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix Obelix All at Sea</a> – haven’t gotten my hands on this one yet, part 2<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122442.Asterix_and_the_Actress__Asterix__31_" title="Asterix and the Actress (Asterix #31) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Actress</a> – haven’t gotten my hands on this one yet, part 3<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71294.Asterix_and_the_Falling_Sky__Asterix__33_" title="Asterix and the Falling Sky (Asterix #33) by Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Falling Sky</a> – a disaster of an Uderzo story; the Gaulish village is visited by competing alien races respectively intended to represent Disney and manga cartoon styles (evenly-matched, you see)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65876.Asterix_and_the_Class_Act__Asterix___32_" title="Asterix and the Class Act (Asterix, #32) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix the Class Act</a> – republication of separately published short stories in a single volume, including a spoof of the fashion trade, a tour de force Mad-style parody of various art/illustration styles, and a hysterically slapstick Christmas joke for which mistletoe plays the catalyst (and told without dialogue!)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Asterix%20vs.%20Caesar" title="Asterix vs. Caesar" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix vs. Caesar</a> – “novelization” of the ‘60s cartoon, itself derived from a combination of the plots of “Legionary,” “Gladiator,” and “Laurel Wreath.” Nothing to see here, move along.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/298050.The_Twelve_Tasks_of_Asterix" title="The Twelve Tasks of Asterix by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">The Twelve Tasks of Asterix</a> – “novelization” of the ‘60s cartoon, based on an original (and funny) plot which spoofs game shows; the Roman Senate challenges A&amp;O to perform 12 Herculean tasks to determine if these Gauls be Gods. Best of the bits is the one that pits Asterix’s wits against bureaucratic futility, but there are other good ones as well.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2895675.Asterix_Conquers_America" title="Asterix Conquers America by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix Conquers America</a> – “novelization” of the ‘60s cartoon, itself derived from “Great Crossing.” Nothing to see here, move along.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/624264.Asterix_Forever___Asterix_and_the_Great_Divide__Asterix_and_the_Magic_Carpet__Operation_Getafix__Asterix_and_the_Secret_Weapon__How_Obelix_fell_into_the_Magic_Potion__Asterix_Conquers_America_" title="Asterix Forever! (Asterix and the Great Divide; Asterix and the Magic Carpet; Operation Getafix; Asterix and the Secret Weapon; How Obelix fell into the Magic Potion; Asterix Conquers America) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Operation Getafix</a> – haven’t gotten my hands on this one yet, part 4, but I understand it to be another “novelization” that combines the plots of “Golden Sickle” and “Goths.” If so, can probably be bypassed without harm.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/621063.How_Obelix_Fell_into_the_Magic_Potion_When_He_Was_a_Little_Boy__Asterix_Comic_" title="How Obelix Fell into the Magic Potion When He Was a Little Boy (Asterix Comic) by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">How Obelix Fell into the Magic Potion When he was a Little Boy</a> - – haven’t gotten my hands on this one yet, part 5 </span>

<div id="review_1279035285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1279035285" />
    <a title="Pramod Nair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37107782-pramod-nair"><img alt="Pramod Nair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425650534p2/37107782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1279035285?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pramod Nair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pramod Nair" href="/user/show/37107782-pramod-nair">Pramod Nair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=childhood-companions">childhood-companions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37107782-pramod-nair?shelf=comic-book">comic-book</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1279035285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6415234225000383331"><i>Ah! Asterix and his picturesque little village in Gaul with its stubborn yet hilarious bunch of residents gave me such a heavy dose of enjoyment during my high school vacation days. </i><br/><br/>Each volume of this series is supremely rich in wonderful cartoon sketches, lots of humor and superb characters. Full marks goes to <i>René Goscinny</i> and <i>Albert Uderzo</i> for creating a bunch of such loveable characters and an exciting series of humorous adventures based on political & historical references. The translation</span>
  <span id="freeText6415234225000383331" style="display:none"><i>Ah! Asterix and his picturesque little village in Gaul with its stubborn yet hilarious bunch of residents gave me such a heavy dose of enjoyment during my high school vacation days. </i><br /><br />Each volume of this series is supremely rich in wonderful cartoon sketches, lots of humor and superb characters. Full marks goes to <i>René Goscinny</i> and <i>Albert Uderzo</i> for creating a bunch of such loveable characters and an exciting series of humorous adventures based on political &amp; historical references. The translations of the original French volumes are done with love and care to make them highly enjoyable.<br /><br />The plots of most of the books in the series revolve around the adventures of Asterix and his fellow villagers – who reside in an unnamed small coastal village in <i>Armorica</i> – against the invading Roman Legionaries; and their village is the last bastion standing in the entire region of Gaul against the mighty Roman Invaders under Julius Caesar. The adventures are set either in the locations around this small village or foreign locations. These adventures of the indomitable Gauls – mainly involving adventures of Asterix and his friend Obelix – thwarting schemes brewed by the Roman forces lead in to one hilarious situation after another, which are portrayed in rich and amazing illustrations and tongue-in-cheek text.<br /> <br />In ‘Asterix the Gaul’ the reader is introduced to the little village of Asterix and it’s assortment of eccentric, funny yet furiously tough residents with witty names. There is the shrewd, cunning little warrior with super human strength named ‘<b>Asterix</b>’; his close buddy ‘<b>Obelix</b>’, who is literally a giant of man with an insatiable appetite for wild boars and massive physical power; the village chief named ‘<b>Vitalstatistix</b>’, who is mighty brave and hot-tempered and widely respected by his people; the village bard named ‘<b>Cacofonix</b>’ whose music is divine for his ears only; the druid of the village named ‘<b>Getafix</b>’, who’s magic potion is the secret behind the superhuman strength of the villagers and ‘<b>Fulliautomatix</b>’ – the village blacksmith; their names along with their antics can make you burst with laughter. When these indomitable villagers are not fighting against the Romans or going on with their daily life which involve a lot bashing each others head, they are busy involved in sumptuous feasts and enjoying the heavenly music of ‘Cacofonix’ by either running away from him or tying him up.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In this first book of this series, ‘<i>Crismus Bonus</i>’, one of the centurions of the invading Roman army finds the secret about the magic potion, which gives super human strength to the Villagers. ‘Crismus Bonus’ plans to steal this secret for his personal agenda of overthrowing Julius Caesar and for that purpose captures Getafix. Asterix infiltrates the Roman garrison to rescue Getafix and the rest of the plot is based on Asterix’s cunning machinations aimed at foiling the plans of ‘Crismus Bonus’. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If you haven’t yet met Asterix and his bunch of friends then taking up his adventures wont disappoint you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6415234225000383331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2096584734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096584734" />
    <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance"><img alt="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600345081p2/53419883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096584734?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096584734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2491155104376923896">This is a goody from my childhood that I haven’t read in years. I guess I felt a little sentimental picking this up.<br/><br/>The Asterix & Obelix comics started being published in 1959 by French authors Rene Goscinny, Albert Uderzo and Jean-Yves Ferri. Since then over 30 books in this series were translated into over 100 languages today. I myself read the German translations as a kid. To this day, boys and girls in Europe are still reading and enjoying these comics as well as the adaptated movies which a</span>
  <span id="freeText2491155104376923896" style="display:none">This is a goody from my childhood that I haven’t read in years. I guess I felt a little sentimental picking this up.<br /><br />The Asterix &amp; Obelix comics started being published in 1959 by French authors Rene Goscinny, Albert Uderzo and Jean-Yves Ferri. Since then over 30 books in this series were translated into over 100 languages today. I myself read the German translations as a kid. To this day, boys and girls in Europe are still reading and enjoying these comics as well as the adaptated movies which are great - those I want to re-watch as well, but guess what, I have them on Beta Max tapes and no player!<br /><br />Asterix and his friends live in a small village in the Roman occupied Gaul around 50 BC. All the occupants of this village are holding out from being invaded by the Roman legions of Julius Caesar. They do this by making a potion that gives them super power, strength and speed. They are already very clever and can outwit anyone before they know it. <br /><br />As the Romans are trying to conquer this last village, they realize something isn’t right about these Gauls that retaliate them albeit being outnumbered. So, they send in a spy to find out what the Gauls are doing to be so strong. But Asterix and his friends are not from yesterday. They know how to fool the Romans and embarrass them at the same time. <br /><br />I enjoyed this clean classic graphic novel. The print of my copy had the original sketches, nothing enhanced, and it was a super quick read. This would be fun for any kid that isn’t addicted to electronics yet or has had a lot of exposure to that. Who doesn’t want to have super powers and play Asterix in the back yard! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2491155104376923896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/51196399-gary">Gary</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3623289764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10801421837048803749">Asterix The Gaul was first published in French in 1961 and in English only in 1969.<br/>The first of the Asterix books , it is a very clever and witty piece of work on the Roman occupation of Gaul in 50 BC-with a fair amount of Latin quips in too -read Asterix and you'll soon become familiar with 'Quid' , 'Vae victo , vae victus' and 'Morituri te salutant'.<br/>It begins with the familiar scene of well thumped Roman legionnaires reporting their defeat to an incensed Roman centurion (in this case Crismus B</span>
  <span id="freeText10801421837048803749" style="display:none">Asterix The Gaul was first published in French in 1961 and in English only in 1969.<br />The first of the Asterix books , it is a very clever and witty piece of work on the Roman occupation of Gaul in 50 BC-with a fair amount of Latin quips in too -read Asterix and you'll soon become familiar with 'Quid' , 'Vae victo , vae victus' and 'Morituri te salutant'.<br />It begins with the familiar scene of well thumped Roman legionnaires reporting their defeat to an incensed Roman centurion (in this case Crismus Bonus) who then hatches a plan to deal with the Gauls which our heroes always in the end foil.<br /><br />It also includes such recurring themes as Cacofonix and his hated singing , the magic potion (and why Obelix cannot have any ) and a guest appearance by Julius Caesar.It ends as always without he Gauls feasting their heroes 'under a starry sky...victorious over their enemies , thanks to magic the protection of the gods and low cunning'.<br /><br />Unlike all of its successors in this book , Obelix does not even offer to accompany Asterix on his adventure (which is so unlike the Obelix we know from all of the other Asterix books).<br />There are some gaps in the dialogue and there is unusually not one woman or girl in the first book . drawbacks which will be made up for in the other Asterix books.<br /><br />Nevertheless it is a great start to your Asterix collection and an amusing little book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10801421837048803749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_312551887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312551887" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312551887?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312551887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7757304431154124930"><b>The first Asterix album</b><br/>14 April 2012<br/><br/>	Now that I have the complete Tintin collection I decided that I would get my hands on the other comic book series that I liked as a child, which surprise, surprise, was Asterix. I am sure many of you already know the premise behind Asterix, but since this is the first of the albums I thought that I might run through it anyway. The story is set in 50BC after Julius Ceaser has conquered Gaul, or almost. There is one little village on the coast of Gaul that just</span>
  <span id="freeText7757304431154124930" style="display:none"><b>The first Asterix album</b><br />14 April 2012<br /><br />	Now that I have the complete Tintin collection I decided that I would get my hands on the other comic book series that I liked as a child, which surprise, surprise, was Asterix. I am sure many of you already know the premise behind Asterix, but since this is the first of the albums I thought that I might run through it anyway. The story is set in 50BC after Julius Ceaser has conquered Gaul, or almost. There is one little village on the coast of Gaul that just does not seem to be able to submit, so the Romans built four camps around the village and attempt to look for a way to bring them under the authority of Rome.<br /><br />	This is the first album and it does show a lot, especially after you have read a lot of the others. In a way it seems very deficient, however we must remember that this is the first and we are seeing an introduction to the characters and the setting. In a way this is something that could only come out of France. It is amusing, silly, and the use of puns is very clever. This is seen a lot more in the later comics, though here the main antagonist, the centurion Crismus Bonus, gave me a good chuckle when I first encountered him.<br /><br />	Most of the comics, when dealing with the little village in Gaul, will only have one of the camps. The four camps are Aquarium, Totorum, Laundanum, and Compendium. The camp that has the focus of this book is Compendium. As you read more and more of the comics you will encounter the style that Goscinny (who wrote the dialogue, Underzo did the drawings) uses. Each of the nationalities have their own little prefix, the Gauls having 'ix' at the end of all of their names (most likely being taken from the Gaul Ubercheiftain Vercingetorix) and all of the Roman's names end in 'us' (most likely taken from the name Julius, though other Romans of note also have a name ending in 'us' though you should note that not all of them follow that convention, though in the books they will generally have two names, such as Calligula Minus, the poor Roman that is picked to spy on the Gauls).<br /><br />	The plot of this comic involves the Romans trying to find out the secret of the Gaul's ability to resist their might, so they disguise a Roman as a Gaul who sneaks into the village, finds the potion, and then returns back to the camp as strong as ever. Upon learning of the potion, they kidnap the druid Getafix (there are lots of puns like this, Vitalstatistix the chief, Fullyautomatix the blacksmith, and Cacofonix the bard). Asterix, who learns of this must then sneak into the camp to get the druid back.<br /><br />	It is rather amusing, especially how the mighty Romans are scared stiffless of the little Gauls, and in many cases Asterix uses his ability to bluff to enable him to get around and reach his goals. Of course, upon learning of the potion, Crismus Bonus decides that to have this power would give him much more influence back in Rome, so decides to go his own way to depose Ceaser and set himself up as dictator. Okay, the history in these stories is really bad, particularly since at this point Ceaser would have been fighting the civil war. There simply did not seem to be a period of peace where Ceaser was ruling unchallenged, but this is a really minor aspect. These comics are not to teach history but to entertain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7757304431154124930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_980544084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/980544084" />
    <a title="Jonatan Iversen-Ejve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11851200-jonatan-iversen-ejve"><img alt="Jonatan Iversen-Ejve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347893102p2/11851200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980544084?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonatan Iversen-Ejve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonatan Iversen-Ejve" href="/user/show/11851200-jonatan-iversen-ejve">Jonatan Iversen-Ejve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11851200-jonatan-iversen-ejve?shelf=asterix">asterix</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980544084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer174499775344511922">Asterix is definitely one of my favorite comic book series of all time. I've only come to like the albums more as I grow older, and seeing as I reread them at least once a year I thought it only right that I take a shot at reviewing them as well. Keep in mind that I read the Swedish editions and might get a few names wrong. I'll try to stick to the English names as much as I can.<br/><br/>So, here goes. Asterix the Gaul is the very first album, and it shows. For me the whole thing always felt like some so</span>
  <span id="freeText174499775344511922" style="display:none">Asterix is definitely one of my favorite comic book series of all time. I've only come to like the albums more as I grow older, and seeing as I reread them at least once a year I thought it only right that I take a shot at reviewing them as well. Keep in mind that I read the Swedish editions and might get a few names wrong. I'll try to stick to the English names as much as I can.<br /><br />So, here goes. Asterix the Gaul is the very first album, and it shows. For me the whole thing always felt like some sort of a trial run before the real series starts, both in art style and storytelling. In fact, you can tell that Uderzo developed his drawing technique throughout the story by comparing the first couple of pages with the last one - characters like Asterix, Getafix and Julius Caesar all look drastically different towards the end, and more like their usual selves that we've come to know.<br />While these books have never been known for very intricate plots, and instead focused more on their humor and cultural satire, this one is probably one of the weakest in terms of story. It revolves around the Romans trying to figure out the secret of the Gauls' great strength, kidnapping the druid Getafix to acquire it for themselves. Asterix comes to the rescue, and the two of them decide to teach the villains a lesson.<br />The biggest "issue" with the main premise of Asterix is that since the main characters have super strength, any form of adversity must be something our heroes can't overcome by simply punching their way through. This is often solved by having them look for some kind of MacGuffin or otherwise face a more intangible problem, so I'm usually completely fine with this. Here, however, the resolution comes relatively early on in the story, with the rest of it mostly consisting of the two Gauls messing around with the Romans just for the heck of it. I might have been fine with it here as well if the story and humor had been enough to save it, but aside from a couple of funny moments it's actually rather dull and unexciting. Likely a huge part of why I'm not very fond of this one overall.<br /><br />So, is there anything good about this album? The pacing is odd, the art style subpar, and Obelix isn't even in half of it! Well... I think it deserves some recognition for being the beginning of something great. The interstellar dust cloud that gave birth to our brightest stars, if you will. Some of the longest running gags can even be found here, like Cacophonix horrible singing or Obelix pouting over not getting any magic potion, and running gags is part of what makes Asterix so brilliant. It's something I will get more into as I continue these reviews, for sure.<br />All in all I wouldn't exactly recommend it to new readers as there are better places to get started, but Asterix fans should definitely give it a read if only to know how it all began.</span>
  <a data-text-id="174499775344511922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1247205989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247205989" />
    <a title="Maria Carmo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3054983-maria-carmo"><img alt="Maria Carmo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261144324p2/3054983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8464432646262496937">It's been a long time coming but I finally got around to starting with the Asterix comics! Asterix the Gaul was hilarious - a classic tale of outwitting the enemy army with sheer cunning (and a little bit of magic, of course), I couldn't help but draw parallels with the grim story of Iron Man and how he escaped his own captors with the help of Ho Yinsen, the scientist to Asterix's Getafix. Except with more than a shade of humor.<br/>Looking forward to rest of the series.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2670552211" />
    <a title="Ill D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5925555-ill-d"><img alt="Ill D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586395253p2/5925555.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ill D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ill D" href="/user/show/5925555-ill-d">Ill D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Wannabe Gentlemen and Scholars</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5925555-ill-d?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5925555-ill-d?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5925555-ill-d?shelf=comic-reviews">comic-reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2670552211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5398660355175937036">I recently sifted my way through the top comic book lists here on Goodreads. I’ve read most of them but I noticed I hadn’t read this classic. Following a quick trip to my local library I finally got my hands on this.<br/><br/>Oh by. What a let down!<br/><br/>Beyond dated, this faux-comic classic spends its first half establishing a minor litany of characters. A buffoonish sidekick, a grizzly old magician and a pint-sized hero, the titular Asterix are presented with pathetically puerile characterizations deserving o</span>
  <span id="freeText5398660355175937036" style="display:none">I recently sifted my way through the top comic book lists here on Goodreads. I’ve read most of them but I noticed I hadn’t read this classic. Following a quick trip to my local library I finally got my hands on this.<br /><br />Oh by. What a let down!<br /><br />Beyond dated, this faux-comic classic spends its first half establishing a minor litany of characters. A buffoonish sidekick, a grizzly old magician and a pint-sized hero, the titular Asterix are presented with pathetically puerile characterizations deserving of the comic’s equally childish art style. All set within the era of the Roman Empire, Asterix makes for a bizarre mish-mash of the slap-stick and the historical. When unfunny humor is followed up by literal Latin, this makes for a jarring read. <br /><br />When compared to such legends as Shultz’s Peanuts or Waterson’s Calvin and Hobbes, Asterix appears neophytic and callow. Subjectively you may or very well may not enjoy the art or politics within either of the aforementioned yet, on an objective level the level of talent and influence cannot be denied Conversely, Asterix has little going for it beyond its induced nostalgia which has propelled it (unfairly I might add) to top comics lists around the world.<br /><br />I still don’t know what the hubbuboo is all about and neither will you once you read my review.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5398660355175937036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205376401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205376401" />
    <a title="Manas Maity" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5869285-manas-maity"><img alt="Manas Maity" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205376401?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manas Maity" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manas Maity" href="/user/show/5869285-manas-maity">Manas Maity</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5869285-manas-maity?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205376401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16630330902094244458">Asterix the Gaul is the first book of a series that took comics to a new height. Since I have read it after enjoying a few others in the series, it is difficult to make an unbiased review of it. However, with the benefit of hindsight it may be said that the characters have 'arrived', but to be properly fleshed out and filled up. Particularly Obelix, who is quite slim, if not so thin. We are sure though that consuming more than one boars at at time, he has made a promising start towards his perso</span>
  <span id="freeText16630330902094244458" style="display:none">Asterix the Gaul is the first book of a series that took comics to a new height. Since I have read it after enjoying a few others in the series, it is difficult to make an unbiased review of it. However, with the benefit of hindsight it may be said that the characters have 'arrived', but to be properly fleshed out and filled up. Particularly Obelix, who is quite slim, if not so thin. We are sure though that consuming more than one boars at at time, he has made a promising start towards his personal fulfillment. The Romans are also immature in their villainy and theatrics and surrender rather 'immaturely'. Again, with the benefit of hindsight it may be said that a good and promising start has been made.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16630330902094244458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089628882" />
    <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter"><img alt="Matthew Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495642903p2/3040804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089628882?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Hunter" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter">Matthew Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=comics-graphic-novels-manga">comics-graphic-novels-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089628882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12893246178540068938">Funny. Smart. Irreverent. I loved it! The punny names work perfectly - a Roman Centurian General named Crismus Bonus, a Centurian of lower rank named Ginantonix, a Druid that provides strength potions to the Gauls named Getafix, a bad bard named Cacofonix. Then there are appetites big enough to eat two entire boars at one sitting. Critical commentary on imperialism and classical civilization. Bright, Looney Tunes-like artwork. It all comes together into something humorous, entertaining, and nice</span>
  <span id="freeText12893246178540068938" style="display:none">Funny. Smart. Irreverent. I loved it! The punny names work perfectly - a Roman Centurian General named Crismus Bonus, a Centurian of lower rank named Ginantonix, a Druid that provides strength potions to the Gauls named Getafix, a bad bard named Cacofonix. Then there are appetites big enough to eat two entire boars at one sitting. Critical commentary on imperialism and classical civilization. Bright, Looney Tunes-like artwork. It all comes together into something humorous, entertaining, and nice to look at. Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12893246178540068938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1099033157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099033157" />
    <a title="Mythili" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10136821-mythili"><img alt="Mythili" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598729724p2/10136821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1099033157?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mythili" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mythili" href="/user/show/10136821-mythili">Mythili</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10136821-mythili?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10136821-mythili?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10136821-mythili?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099033157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12903437930971588776">Years ago my dad bought the entire collection of Asterix and I had read most of them. Even though I remember the plotlines and the hilarious names, rereading is just as much fun! There is never a dull moment and the situations are so excessively hilarious that I find myself shutting the book to laugh for a good couple of minutes and resuming a moment later. <br/><br/>As far as comics go, Asterix is the best when it comes to historical and political satire. I would recommend this to pretty much anyone. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mRgNME7MkwgeZeX3DJW5ev3g26L9Cxj1cFwdTBXu2mHQwA1WiCUO/mlkYxZtbjwOukF+B86NztBmA3IHr74DpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/wp2VCp/nL1gk8tWnWgrYArAYHNSVYpdpszgyFXeYg620nYy7JYBSxeSTbf8k64UTWHF1mHTXHiwk4+D7467yw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9050822353936023623">René Goscinny (1926 - 1977) was a French author, editor and humorist, who is best known for the comic book <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41270-asterix' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asterix</a>
</i>, which he created with illustrator <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26082.Albert_Uderzo' title='Albert Uderzo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Albert Uderzo</a>, and for his work on the comic series <i>Lucky Luke</i> with Morris (considered the series' golden age).</span>
  <span id="freeText9050822353936023623" style="display:none">René Goscinny (1926 - 1977) was a French author, editor and humorist, who is best known for the comic book <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41270-asterix" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix</a>
</i>, which he created with illustrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26082.Albert_Uderzo" title="Albert Uderzo" rel="nofollow noopener">Albert Uderzo</a>, and for his work on the comic series <i>Lucky Luke</i> with Morris (considered the series' golden age).</span>
